Report on Critical Issues within the Criminal Justice System:
Analysis of Benjamin Allen Case File

Executive Summary
This report presents a comprehensive analysis of the Allen case file, revealing numerous critical failures and misconduct throughout various stages of the criminal justice process.
The identified issues encompass judicial oversight, investigative procedures, prosecutorial conduct, evidence handling, defense representation, and systemic vulnerabilities.
These failures raise significant concerns about due process, fair trial rights, and the potential for wrongful convictions.
This document underscores specific procedural lapses, ethical violations, and intentional misconduct, highlighting the urgent need for systemic reforms and a thorough case review.
Investigative Failures and Detective Misconduct
Benjamin S. Allen Case: Systemic Breakdown
This case is emblematic of a profound systemic failure characterized by alleged misconduct, significant investigative lapses, and ineffective legal counsel.
Detective Bias: The investigation was demonstrably biased, compromising the impartiality and thoroughness expected in criminal proceedings.
Evidence Mishandling: Evidence mishandling raises questions about the integrity and reliability of the evidence presented.
Formal Misconduct Complaints: To underscore the severity of the ethical and procedural concerns, formal complaints must be filed against the investigating detective and Assistant District Attorney for professional misconduct.
Systemic Reform Imperative: These failures are not isolated incidents but point to systemic issues within the Lee County Sherrif’s Department and Lee County judicial frameworks, necessitating broader reforms to prevent future miscarriages of justice.
This situation presents serious constitutional and legal challenges.
Prosecutorial Misconduct
ADA (Assistant District Attorney) Issues: Ethical Lapses
The Assistant District Attorney's (ADA) conduct reveals multiple instances of prosecutorial misconduct, undermining the fairness and impartiality of the legal process.
Procedural Abuse: Excessive Continuances: The case was subjected to excessive continuances – 37 times over four years – constituting procedural abuse and causing undue hardship to the defendant, including the loss of evidence critical to the case.
Discovery Violations: Discovery violations further prejudiced against the defendant's defense ability.
Due Process Violations: Fair Trial Infringement
Cumulative Violations: The combination of discovery violations, lost evidence, and excessive delays collectively infringed upon the defendant's fundamental right to a fair trial and due process as guaranteed by the Constitution.
Evidence Collection and Handling Issues
Serious Evidence Collection Failures: Procedural Negligence
Significant failures in evidence collection and handling highlight systemic weaknesses in investigative procedures.
Crime Scene Neglect: Failure to collect evidence from crime scenes and inadequate crime-scene investigation procedures demonstrate a lack of thoroughness.
Chain of Custody Problems: Breakdowns in the chain of custody for evidence compromise the integrity and admissibility of collected materials.
Defense Representation Issues
Ineffective Assistance of Counsel: Attorney Deficiencies
The defendant suffered from ineffective assistance of counsel, significantly undermining their ability to receive a fair defense.
Jury Impact: These failures negatively impacted the jury's verdict, prejudicing the trial's outcome.
Attorney Conflict of Interest: A critical conflict of interest existed because the attorney had a previous relationship with the detective, which compromised the attorney's impartiality and effectiveness.
Defense Representation Issues
Ineffective Assistance of Counsel
In this case, erroneous convictions were not due to single errors but resulted from a compounding effect of initial investigative mistakes exacerbated by subsequent failures throughout the legal process.
Inadequate Defense Preparation: Defense attorneys failed to prepare adequate defenses, weakening the defendant's position.
Prosecutorial Misconduct Following Initial Errors: Prosecutorial misconduct compounded the initial investigative errors, creating a cascade of injustice.
Brady Violations: Exculpatory Evidence Suppression
Brady violations refer to instances where prosecutors fail to disclose material evidence favorable to the defendant, as established by the landmark Supreme Court case Brady v. Maryland (373 U.S. 83, 1963).
This ruling established that suppression of evidence favorable to an accused violates due process when the evidence is material either to guilt or punishment, regardless of the prosecution's good faith or bad faith.
Key Legal Principles Related to Brady Violations
Basic Obligation: The prosecution must disclose all favorable, material evidence to the defense, even without a specific request from the defendant.
Types of Evidence That Must Be Disclosed:
Evidence that tends to negate guilt
Evidence that mitigates an offense or potential sentence
Impeachment evidence that affects witness credibility
Evidence discrediting police investigation or officers' credibility


Materiality Standard: Evidence is considered material "if there is a reasonable probability that, had the evidence been disclosed to the defense, the result of the proceeding would have been different" (United States v. Bagley, 473 U.S. 667, 682, 1985).
Timing of Disclosure: The prosecution must provide Brady material in time for the defendant to effectively use it at trial.
Evidence Need Not Be Admissible: The prosecution must disclose favorable, material evidence, even if it would be inadmissible at trial, as long as it could lead to admissible evidence.
Legal Basis: Napue v. Illinois established that prosecutors violate defendants' due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment when allowing false testimony to go uncorrected.
Misuse of Grand Jury Processes
The ADA persists in employing grand jury practices explicitly declared unconstitutional, such as introducing misleading evidence and false testimony.
Legal Basis: Misleading a grand jury or knowingly introducing false evidence violates a defendant's Fifth Amendment right to due process and fair proceedings.
Such misuse directly undermines the integrity of the judicial process, constituting actionable prosecutorial misconduct under §1983.
Violation of Established Brady Obligations
The prosecutors' obligations to disclose exculpatory evidence (Brady v. Maryland), the ADA deliberately withholds such evidence, depriving defendants of their right to a fair trial.
Legal Basis: Withholding exculpatory evidence violates Brady v. Maryland and subsequent decisions (e.g., Giglio v. United States), infringing on defendants’ Fourteenth Amendment rights to due process and fair trial.
Prosecutorial misconduct of this type is explicitly actionable.
Failure to Comply with Declared Right to Speedy Trial
The ADA denied the defendant’s right to a speedy trial by unnecessarily delaying, depriving the defendant of timely adjudication and fundamental procedural fairness.
Legal Basis: The Sixth Amendment unequivocally establishes defendants' right to a speedy trial, as reinforced by Barker v. Wingo.
Intentional or unnecessary prosecutorial delays explicitly violate this fundamental constitutional protection.
Abuse of Plea-Bargaining Processes
ADA lied about evidence and inflated charges, creating harsher penalties to induce a guilty plea.
Legal Basis: Prosecutors violate due process under the Fourteenth Amendment when engaging in coercive or fraudulent plea-bargaining tactics.
Lying about evidence or inflating charges to coerce guilty pleas directly violates constitutional guarantees of fairness and voluntariness in criminal proceedings.
Denial of Constitutional Rights to Discovery
The ADA denied the defendant access to critical discovery materials, violating the defendant’s constitutional right to comprehensive pre-trial discovery.
Legal Basis: Denial of discovery materials necessary for defense violates defendants' rights to a fair trial under the Sixth Amendment and due process under the Fourteenth Amendment.
Such violations explicitly contravene precedents established by Brady, which requires comprehensive disclosure of exculpatory evidence.
Legal Principal Violations: This manipulation violated several fundamental legal principles:
Hearsay rules
Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment
Best Evidence Rule
Authentication requirements
8.
Specific Legal Concerns: This conflict directly infringed upon:
Fourth Amendment protections against unreasonable searches and seizures.
Fourteenth Amendment due process clause.
Legal precedent established in Giglio v. United States regarding the mandatory disclosure of witness credibility issues.
Rushed and Incomplete Investigation: Insufficient Legal Basis
Premature Capital Offense Charge: The detective charged the suspect with a capital offense after a mere four-hour investigation, demonstrating a rush to judgment without proper evidentiary foundation.
Violation of Probable Cause Standard: This rushed approach violated the established legal standard for probable cause as defined in Illinois v. Gates, which requires a comprehensive "totality of the circumstances" analysis.
Aggravating Factor Manipulation: After the defendant refused to accept the plea, the ADA returned to the Grand Jury to introduce an aggravating factor, suggesting retaliatory and unethical tactics.
Violations of Chain of Custody Procedures
Evidence Handling Failures: Integrity Compromised
Chain of Custody Breaches: Significant failures in maintaining proper chain of custody for evidence were identified, compromising the integrity of evidentiary materials.
Specific Failures: These breaches included:
Improper securing of evidence.
Violation of Speedy Trial Rights
Excessive Continuances: Due Process Erosion
Unjustified Delays: The prosecution's continuing the case 37 times over four years is highly unusual and represents an egregious abuse of court resources and process.
Harmful Impacts of Delays: This persistent delay tactic resulted in:
Severe emotional distress to the defendant.
Impairment of the defendant's ability to adequately prepare for trial.
Potential prejudice against the defendant in the eyes of the jury.
Legal Standard Ignored: These delays contravene the principles established in Barker v. Wingo, emphasizing that deliberate attempts to delay trials should be heavily weighted against the prosecution.
Prejudicial Impact of Prolonged Case
Economic and Emotional Harm: Defendant Prejudice
Significant Prejudice: The defendant suffered substantial prejudice due to the prolonged case duration.
Specific Harms: These included:
Complete loss of income for the defendant, a single father, throughout the protracted legal proceedings.
Immediate job termination and inability to secure new employment without attorney approval, causing severe financial strain.
Loss of critical evidence by the defendant's attorneys during the extended timeframe, hampering the defense.
Denial of Right to Assert Speedy Trial Claims
Ignored Constitutional Rights: Attorney Negligence
Sixth Amendment Rights Ignored: The defendant's repeated attempts to assert his Sixth Amendment right to a speedy trial were actively thwarted as his attorneys refused to file the necessary motions.
Misinformation to Defendant: The defendant was repeatedly misinformed that his Sixth Amendment rights were not applicable, demonstrating a profound misunderstanding or deliberate misrepresentation of constitutional law by his legal counsel.
Consequences of Bias: This bias led to:
Failure to comprehensively gather and impartially evaluate all available evidence.
Active disregard of evidence that could potentially exonerate the defendant.
Possible attempt to conceal law enforcement actions during the unaccounted hour.
Coordination among multiple conspirators, pointing to a deliberate plan.
Ethical Misconduct in Handling Exculpatory Evidence
Attorneys Concealing Exculpatory Evidence: Legal Ethics Breach
Exculpatory Evidence Withholding: The defendant's attorney failed to disclose bribery text messages to the sheriff's office, representing a serious breach of legal ethics.
Potential Obstruction of Justice: This failure to disclose potentially constitutes obstruction of justice, further compounding the ethical violations.
Overcharging as Prosecutorial Strategy
Deliberate Misrepresentation to Grand Jury: Abusive Tactics
Plea Deal Misunderstanding Admission: The ADA admitted, in the presence of a judge and attorneys, offering a plea deal based on a misunderstanding of the evidence, yet continued to pursue charges.
Specific Violations: These procedural failures included:
Failure to document probable cause for arrest.
Not bringing the defendant before a magistrate for prompt judicial review.
Using a retrospective order to justify detention after it had already occurred.
Officer's Statement of Role to "Prove Guilt"
Explicit Bias from Law Enforcement: Impartiality Compromised
Bias Statement: An officer was recorded stating that their job was to "prove guilt," openly demonstrating a blatant violation of the fundamental duty to be fair and impartial in investigations.
Evidence of Misconduct: This statement is direct evidence of police misconduct and bias against the defendant, undermining the investigation's integrity.
Systemic Corruption in the Justice System
Network of Improper Relationships: Systemic Integrity Concerns
Improper Network: Detective Freeman's documented connection to the defendant's attorney and their history of collaborative casework suggest a potential network of improper relationships.
Influence on the Justice System: This network raises serious concerns about potential undue influence and systemic corruption within the local justice system, which could impact case outcomes and fairness.
Further Ethical Violation: This action represents a further violation of ethical obligations and a deliberate attempt to mislead the jury with false information from the outset of the trial.
Appearance of Concealment: This loss of evidence represents a serious breakdown in evidence handling and creates a strong appearance of deliberate concealment of potentially exculpatory information.
This suggests evidence being introduced after the fact without adherence to proper documentation or chain of custody protocols.
Hospital Officials Failure to Follow Protocol
Medical Record Irregularities: Protocol Breaches
Mandatory Reporting Concerns: Testimony regarding events at Central Carolina Hospital (CCH) raises serious concerns about whether hospital officials properly adhered to mandatory reporting laws for sexual assault cases.
Transparency Compromised: Withholding these critical emergency records undermines transparency and public trust in the investigation process.
Conclusion
The cumulative effect of these identified issues paints a disturbing picture of systemic failures, procedural violations, and potential misconduct within the criminal justice process in this case.
From judicial oversights to investigative biases, prosecutorial overreach, evidence mishandling, and inadequate defense representation, nearly every stage of the process exhibits critical flaws.
The sheer volume and severity of these issues underscore a profound miscarriage of justice and necessitate immediate, comprehensive review and systemic reforms to prevent future occurrences and ensure that principles of fairness, due process, and constitutional rights are upheld for all individuals within the justice system.
This case demands a thorough re-examination and appropriate corrective actions to restore faith in the integrity of the legal process.

Report on Critical Issues within the Criminal Justice System:
Analysis of Benjamin Allen Case File

Executive Summary
This report provides a detailed analysis of the Allen case file, identifying critical failures and potential misconduct at various stages of the criminal justice process.
The issues include investigative procedures, prosecutorial conduct, evidence handling, defense representation, and systemic vulnerabilities.
These raise concerns about due process, fair trial rights, and the potential for wrongful convictions.
This document outlines procedural lapses and ethical concerns, emphasizing the need for systemic reforms and a comprehensive case review.1
Notably, the trial resulted in a mistrial due to a hung jury (unanimous not guilty on first-degree forcible rape; 9-3 split on second-degree forcible rape after approximately 7 hours of deliberation).
There was no conviction, and given the evidentiary weaknesses and procedural issues, a retrial may raise double jeopardy concerns or questions of prosecutorial discretion under principles from Oregon v. Kennedy, 456 U.S. 667 (1982) (mistrial due to prosecutorial misconduct bars retrial if intended to provoke it).
The case highlights broader systemic problems in Lee County, North Carolina, warranting an independent review.
July 10, 2023: Trial begins; witnesses testify (e.g., Deal, Freeman).
Investigative Failures and Detective Misconduct
This case highlights systemic failures, including potential investigative oversights and conflicts of interest.2
Detective Bias: The investigation raises concerns about impartiality due to apparent oversights in witness selection and evidence collection, including an undisclosed familial relationship between Detective Freeman and key witness Carmen Love (his family member), creating a conflict of interest that violated ethical standards under North Carolina State Bar Rule 1.7 and potentially due process under the Fourteenth Amendment.3
Evidence Mishandling: Evidence was not collected or preserved properly (e.g., no DNA from the crime scene beyond photos; pants collected that were claimed to be the claimant's but never tested; chain-of-custody breaks requiring replacement documents at trial), raising integrity concerns under N.C. Gen. Stat.
§ 15A-268.4
Formal Misconduct Complaints: Given the procedural issues, consider filing complaints with the North Carolina State Bar under Rule 8.3 (reporting professional misconduct) against Freeman and the ADA.5
Systemic Reform Imperative: These issues suggest broader problems in the Lee County Sheriff’s Department, warranting reforms such as mandatory conflict disclosures and evidence training per N.C. Gen. Stat.
Procedural deficiencies include no magistrate review post-arrest, violating Fourth Amendment due process.15
Failure to Collect/Preserve Evidence: No physical samples from the scene (e.g., bedding); used a lack of evidence against Allen (e.g., insinuating garbage bags hid items).
This violates speedy trial rights under Barker v. Wingo, 407 U.S. 514 (1972).19
Discovery Violations: Medical records delayed until trial day; exculpatory evidence suppressed (e.g., video contradictions, extortion motive), constituting Brady violations under Kyles v. Whitley, 514 U.S. 419 (1995).20
Misuse of Grand Jury: False claims (e.g., sperm/DNA presence) presented, violating due process under Napue.21
Failure to Correct False Testimony: Allowed Freeman's perjured claims of not knowing possible witnesses and arrest claims to stand.22
Abuse of Plea-Bargaining: Lied about evidence to coerce plea; retaliatory aggravating factor added.23
Evidence Collection and Handling Issues
Crime Scene Neglect: No evidence collected beyond photos; pants untested for ownership/gender.
Exculpatory Evidence Suppression
Brady violations through non-disclosure of material evidence (e.g., Love's fabrications, video, or extortion), meeting the materiality standard under United States v. Bagley, 473 U.S. 667 (1985).
Tied to the Barker prejudice factor.30

Rule 607. Who may impeach.
– If, while testifying, a witness uses a writing or object to refresh his memory, an adverse party is entitled to have the writing or object produced at the trial, hearing, or deposition in which the witness is testifying.
– If, before testifying, a witness uses a writing or object to refresh his memory for the purpose of testifying and the court in its discretion determines that the interests of justice so require, an adverse party is entitled to have those portions of any writing or of the object which relate to the testimony produced, if practicable, at the trial, hearing, or deposition in which the witness is testifying.
– A party entitled to have a writing or object produced under this rule is entitled to inspect it, to cross‑examine the witness thereon, and to introduce in evidence those portions which relate to the testimony of the witness.
If production of the writing or object at the trial, hearing, or deposition is impracticable, the court may order it made available for inspection.
If it is claimed that the writing or object contains privileged information or information not directly related to the subject matter of the testimony, the court shall examine the writing or object in camera, excise any such portions, and order delivery of the remainder to the party entitled thereto.
Any portion withheld over objections shall be preserved and made available to the appellate court in the event of an appeal.
If a writing or object is not produced, made available for inspection, or delivered pursuant to order under this rule, the court shall make any order justice requires, but in criminal cases if the prosecution elects not to comply, the order shall be one striking the testimony or, if justice so requires, declaring a mistrial.
Although relevant, evidence may be excluded if its probative value is substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice, confusion of the issues, or misleading the jury, or by considerations of undue delay, waste of time, or needless presentation of cumulative evidence.
To prove the content of a writing, recording, or photograph, the original writing, recording, or photograph is required, except as otherwise provided in these rules or by statute.
Admissibility of duplicates.
– An "original" of a writing or recording is the writing or recording itself or any counterpart intended to have the same effect by a person executing or issuing it.

Limitations on Warrantless Arrests
However, there are important restrictions:
For most misdemeanors not committed in an officer's presence, a warrant is required12.
Officers generally need a warrant to enter a home to make an arrest, with some exceptions like exigent circumstances or hot pursuit23.
A warrant is required to enter a third party's home to make an arrest3.
Concerns with Frequent Warrantless Arrests
A sheriff's deputy making many warrantless arrests could raise several issues:
Potential Fourth Amendment violations if arrests are made without proper probable cause or in situations requiring a warrant5.
Risk of evidence being thrown out in court if arrests are found to be unlawful.
Possible pattern of overreach or disregard for proper procedures.
Proper Procedure
The standard practice for law enforcement should be:
Obtain warrants when required, especially for misdemeanors not witnessed and for entering homes.
Make warrantless arrests only when legally justified and with clear probable cause.
Document the justification for any warrantless arrests thoroughly.
If a sheriff's deputy is consistently making warrantless arrests outside these guidelines, it would be concerning and potentially indicate a need for additional training or supervision to ensure compliance with legal requirements and protection of individuals' rights.
First Amendment Bearing on Probable Cause and Particularity
The right of the people to be secure in their persons, houses, papers, and effects, against unreasonable searches and seizures, shall not be violated, and no Warrants shall issue but upon probable cause, supported by Oath or affirmation, and particularly describing the place to be searched, and the persons or things to be seized.
Annotations
First Amendment Bearing on Probable Cause and Particularity.—Where the warrant process is used to authorize seizure of books and other items that may be protected by the First Amendment, the Court has required government to observe more exacting standards than in other cases.135 Seizure of materials arguably protected by the First Amendment is a form of prior restraint that requires strict observance of the Fourth Amendment.
At a minimum, a warrant is required, and additional safeguards may be required for large-scale seizures.
Thus, in Marcus v. Search Warrant,136 the seizure of 11,000 copies of 280 publications pursuant to warrant issued ex parte by a magistrate who had not examined any of the publications but who had relied on the conclusory affidavit of a policeman was voided.
Failure to scrutinize the materials and to particularize the items to be seized was deemed inadequate, and it was further noted that police “were provided with no guide to the exercise of informed discretion, because there was no step in the procedure before seizure designed to focus searchingly on the question of obscenity.”137 A state procedure that was designed to comply with Marcus by the presentation of copies of books to be seized to the magistrate for his scrutiny prior to issuance of a warrant was nonetheless found inadequate by a plurality of the Court, which concluded that “since the warrant here authorized the sheriff to seize all copies of the specified titles, and since appellant was not afforded a hearing on the question of the obscenity even of the seven novels seven of 59 listed titles were reviewed by the magistrate before the warrant issued, the procedure was .
constitutionally deficient.”138
Confusion remains, however, about the necessity for and the character of prior adversary hearings on the issue of obscenity.
In a later decision the Court held that, with adequate safeguards, no preseizure adversary hearing on the issue of obscenity is required if the film is seized not for the purpose of destruction as contraband (the purpose in Marcus and A Quantity of Books), but instead to preserve a copy for evidence.139 It is constitutionally permissible to seize a copy of a film pursuant to a warrant as long as there is a prompt post-seizure adversary hearing on the obscenity issue.
Until there is a judicial determination of obscenity, the Court advised, the film may continue to be exhibited; if no other copy is available either a copy of it must be made from the seized film or the film itself must be returned.140
The seizure of a film without the authority of a constitutionally sufficient warrant is invalid; seizure cannot be justified as incidental to arrest, as the determination of obscenity may not be made by the officer himself.141 Nor may a warrant issue based “solely on the conclusory assertions of the police officer without any inquiry by the magistrate into the factual basis for the officer’s conclusions.”142 Instead, a warrant must be “supported by affidavits setting forth specific facts in order that the issuing magistrate may ‘focus searchingly on the question of obscenity.’”143 This does not mean, however, that a higher standard of probable cause is required in order to obtain a warrant to seize materials protected by the First Amendment.
of reasonableness’ was not intended to establish a ‘higher’ standard of probable cause for the issuance of a warrant to seize books or films, but instead related to the more basic requirement, imposed by that decision, that the police not rely on the ‘exigency’ exception to the Fourth Amendment warrant requirement, but instead obtain a warrant from a magistrate .
.’”144
In Stanford v. Texas,145 the Court voided a seizure of more than 2,000 books, pamphlets, and other documents pursuant to a warrant that merely authorized the seizure of books, pamphlets, and other written instruments “concerning the Communist Party of Texas.” “The constitutional requirement that warrants must particularly describe the ‘things to be seized’ is to be accorded the most scrupulous exactitude when the ‘things’ are books, and the basis for their seizure is the ideas which they contain.
No less a standard could be faithful to First Amendment freedoms.”146
However, the First Amendment does not bar the issuance or execution of a warrant to search a newsroom to obtain photographs of demonstrators who had injured several policemen, although the Court appeared to suggest that a magistrate asked to issue such a warrant should guard against interference with press freedoms through limits on type, scope, and intrusiveness of the search.147

For First Amendment implications of seizures under the Federal Racketeer Inﬂuenced and Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO), see First Amendment: Obscenity and Prior Restraint.

– A "duplicate" is a counterpart produced by the same impression as the original, or from the same matrix, or by means of photography, including enlargements and miniatures, or by mechanical or electronic re‑recording, or by chemical reproduction, or by other equivalent techniques which accurately reproduce the original.

Work History
Continually performed within the top 15% of Agency employees
Received multiple awards, including 2 Superior Civilian Awards, while deployed to active war zones.
Extensive experience in developing multifunctional teams to solve Department of Defense (DoD) issues impacting the DoD Digital Modernization Strategy
Advisor to C-level equivalent (General/SES) for over ten years
Ability to coordinate integration efforts across multiple DoD components.
I have held a Top Secret / Sensitive Compartmented Information for over 20 years.
SCI clearance investigations involve an additional screening process.
Not everyone with a Top Secret (TS) clearance has SCI access.
You are only eligible for SCI screening if specific duties require access to this information.
This required Single Scope Background Investigations, which are extensive background checks and investigation processes that can take several months or even years to complete.
A single-scope background investigation (SSBI) is the most comprehensive investigation that the government can conduct, in addition to interviews and reviews of financial, criminal, and medical records.
It is designed to assess honesty and integrity by measuring various physiological responses while answering several questions.
I also held additional clearance levels reserved for individuals requiring access to sensitive or compartmented information.
These include Special Access Programs (SAP) created for specific government projects or programs requiring additional screening.
These Control System caveats included GAMMA, TALENT KEYHOLE, HUMINT, and SI.
SI / GAMMA - This sub-control system of SI is for highly sensitive communication intercepts (product or content) * and, therefore, requires the ORCON dissemination marking.
GAMMA may contain compartments identified by a codeword or an identifier of four alphabetic characters.
HUMINT/HCS -This control system is intended to provide enhanced protection to exceptionally fragile clandestine HUMINT sources, methods, and activities based on assessed value, critical nature, and information vulnerability.
TALENT KEYHOLE – Covers space-based IMINT (imagery intelligence), SIGINT (signals intelligence), and MASINT (measurement and signature intelligence) collection platforms; related processing and analysis techniques; and research, design, and operation of these platforms.

Summary of current investigation:
On 12/01/2014, Lee County DSS received report with concerns of sexual abuse by father towards Lukas.
According to the report, Mother took the recorded material to Lee County Sheriff.
On 12/4/2014, the children were again interviewed by Lee County social workers with similar outcomes.
A Child Family Evaluation (CFE) was done.
Lee County Sheriff and DA were notified.
On 2/9/15 and 2/11/15 all four children were taken for CME at Triangle CAPs.
After evaluation the doctor on site found no indication of bites or parasites.
Doctor diagnosed 6-month-old child as having diaper rash.
Criminal History of Parents:
Mother: Tiffany Allen

--- FILE: E:/Organization_Folder/02_Working_Folder/02_Analysis/06_Case Review\Case Introduction Allen Benjamin_20260201_193935.docx ---
I wanted to start a little better than I did with my last attorney.
Even on the last day of court, he still called me a contractor.
I will attempt to communicate more effectively to ensure that I am not wasting your time looking through materials to ascertain answers that I should have provided upfront.
Work History
Continually performed within the top 15% of Agency employees
Received multiple awards, including 2 Superior Civilian Awards, while deployed to active war zones.
Extensive experience in developing multifunctional teams to solve Department of Defense (DoD) issues impacting the DoD Digital Modernization Strategy
Advisor to C-level equivalent (General/SES) for over ten years
Ability to coordinate integration efforts across multiple DoD components.
I have held a Top Secret / Sensitive Compartmented Information for over 20 years.
SCI clearance investigations involve an additional screening process.
Not everyone with a Top Secret (TS) clearance has SCI access.
You are only eligible for SCI screening if specific duties require access to this information.
This required Single Scope Background Investigations, which are extensive background checks and investigation processes that can take several months or even years to complete.
A single-scope background investigation (SSBI) is the most comprehensive investigation that the government can conduct, in addition to interviews and reviews of financial, criminal, and medical records.
It is designed to assess honesty and integrity by measuring various physiological responses while answering several questions.
I also held additional clearance levels reserved for individuals requiring access to sensitive or compartmented information.
These include Special Access Programs (SAP) created for specific government projects or programs requiring additional screening.
These Control System caveats included GAMMA, TALENT KEYHOLE, HUMINT, and SI.
SI / GAMMA - This sub-control system of SI is for highly sensitive communication intercepts (product or content) * and, therefore, requires the ORCON dissemination marking.
GAMMA may contain compartments identified by a codeword or an identifier of four alphabetic characters.
HUMINT/HCS -This control system is intended to provide enhanced protection to exceptionally fragile clandestine HUMINT sources, methods, and activities based on assessed value, critical nature, and information vulnerability.
TALENT KEYHOLE – Covers space-based IMINT (imagery intelligence), SIGINT (signals intelligence), and MASINT (measurement and signature intelligence) collection platforms; related processing and analysis techniques; and research, design, and operation of these platforms.
PROFESSIONAL EXPERIENCE
NATIONAL GEOSPATIAL-INTELLIGENCE AGENCY, SPRINGFIELD, VA
Intelligence Officer / Government Employee, May 2009 – Present
• Coach, teach, and mentor a team of technical professionals in support of the National Defense Strategy (NDS).
• Advisor to leadership for building a secure, coordinated, seamless, transparent, and effective IT architecture that transforms data into actionable information and dependable mission execution.
• Led the effort on integrating technologies into multiple Mission Command systems, including Command Post of the Future (CPOF), Automated Information Discovery Environment (AIDE /ARES), and the Army’s Command Post Computing Environment (CP CE) with coordination across multiple organizations such as INSCOM, NGA, AGC, and other Department of Defense components.
KENNEDY IRREGULAR WARFARE CENTER, SUITLAND, MD
Senior Engineer, June 2006 – May 2009
• Functioned as the lead engineer within the Kennedy Irregular Warfare Center and Subject Matter Expert for Geospatial Intelligence within the Office of Naval Intelligence • Developed innovative methods to support personnel in support of Naval Special Warfare (NSW) • Selected from a diverse cadre of multi-discipline intelligence professionals to represent the organization at multiple high-level decision-making meetings to include one on one demonstration at the Pentagon to the Director of Naval Intelligence.
SKYLINE SOFTWARE SYSTEMS, HERNDON, VA
Senior Engineer – Consulting – Various (2007-2009)
• Evaluate software from multiple companies to check for interoperability and possible integration.
• Assist clients in designing and implementing the infrastructure to support production and sustainability from development to operation.
• Defines client’s needs and required functionality for inclusion into the company’s product line.
These customers included the Defense Threat Reduction Agency and the Defense Intelligence Agency

UNITED STATES MARINE CORPS, MARINE CORPS INTELLIGENCE ACTIVITY, VA
Marine - Intelligence, Apr 2001 – Jun 2006

UNITED STATES MARINE CORPS, CAMP LEJEUNE, NC
Marine - Intelligence, Nov 1998 – Apr 2001

E D U C A T I O N
National Geospatial-Intelligence College
Various DoD-specific training to include Hyperspectral, Remote Sensing, Geographic Information Systems, Geomatics, Windows Administration, Intelligence and Security
(See attachments)

Bryan Kirkpatrick	Jorge Morales

FAMILY BACKGROUND
I was told by my first attorney (Frank Collins) that this would never have been tried if it hadn’t been for statements made by Tiffany Allen.
We have a long history in the Family Courts in Lee County.
I turned the phone over to my attorney.
It was misplaced during the transition between lawyers in the firm after the State asked for 37 continuances.
I am unable to work due to the requirements placed on me by the government, so the ADA used this to drain my resources.
I am a single father struggling to support two children with no income.
I still had the examples I sent to my first attorney, but that is all.
I will include snapshots that I sent to my first attorney.
I would pass over the phone and data, but this was misplaced by my attorneys at some point over the past few years.
Brendan Allen – (484)929-6524
Carter Olson – (507)822-8214
Morgan and Lukas still live with me, but I could have made them available if they had even thought to ask.
Former Family Law Paralegal at Wilson, Reives, Silverman & Doran, PLLC.
Worked for the local government since 2013.
He is a building inspector for the local government.
His father works with the police department.
The request was entered on Dec 9th, 2019.
The ADA, my attorneys, and the judge had to track them down the day of court.
I told my attorney that this was impossible.
The ADA, my attorneys, and the judge sat down to discuss.
The ADA was informed that the expert had a set time to leave because he had surgery scheduled.
The ADA said that there would be plenty of time before then.
Even with the expert being provided, I was still disadvantaged.
I asked my attorneys if they had billed me for time working on the DNA.
I told them I didn’t have any additional resources to spend.
My job was taken away once I was charged.
How was their time being taken away from other avenues of my defense not a disadvantage for me?
The ADA continually delayed turning over documents such as medical records.
A search warrant was served to retrieve an item from my property even after my attorney was informed that it was there, and I was told that the ADA would be contacted to retrieve it.
Other trash from the back of my vehicle was represented as something nefarious, even though they never bothered to retrieve the trash that had been saved for them from the residence or took the trash they tried to represent as evidence.
My attorneys never addressed this, even though I repeatedly sent the property overview and asked where she ran to.
One of the gentleman's father works with the police department.
The other also works in some capacity for the city.
A request to retrieve all email communications and telephone calls from this time period would be appropriate.
The second lesser included charge, the vote was 9-3, both in favor of acquittal.

--- FILE: E:/Organization_Folder/02_Working_Folder/02_Analysis/06_Case Review\Case Summary - State v Benjamin Allen - Bartholomew.docx ---
INTRODUCTION TO CHARACTERS
Benjamin Allen – Accused
Lauren Deal - Accuser
Carmen Love -  She spent the evening drinking with Deal at Goodfellas and Schooley’s.
Former Family Law Paralegal at Wilson, Reives, Silverman & Doran, PLLC.
Worked for the local government since 2013 and worked with the detective's brother.
He is a building inspector for the local government.
His father works with the police department.
His father took custody of me the morning I made bail.
Frank Collins – First Attorney
Jason Wunsch – Second Attorney / Knew the detective, so didn’t examine him on the stand
Freddie Cruz – Second Attorney
Detective Steve Freeman – Network of friends with accusing party 

ADA Tiffany Bartholomew:
-Lives in Pinehurst, North Carolina.
From Alexandria, Virginia
-Currently an ADA in Lee County, NC
-Previous ADA in Moore County, NC ~10 years
-During her tenure at Moore County, they had one the highest conviction rates for Sexual Assault in the state.
- Governor Roy Cooper appointed Tiffany Bartholomew, of Pinehurst, as District Court Judge serving Moore and Hoke Counties in 2019.
When I was asked to come back in by my attorney’s assistant, I told them that they could all go fuck themselves.
I can at least sit out here and smoke while y’all fuck me.”
They went upstairs to discuss it with the judge and the ADA in chambers.
The following is a summary of events that encapsulate this issue.
I believe this should be reviewed to determine how this conclusion was reached.
The ADA used multiple underhanded techniques during that time.
These include not turning over documents when agreed and not responding to inquiries promptly.
The request was entered on Dec 9th, 2019.
The ADA, my attorneys, and the judge had to track them down the day of court.
I told my attorney that this was impossible.
The ADA, my attorneys, and the judge sat down to discuss.
The ADA was informed that the expert had a set time to leave because he had surgery scheduled.
The ADA said that there would be plenty of time before then.
Even with the expert being provided, I was still disadvantaged.
I asked my attorneys if they had billed me for time working on the DNA.
I told them I didn’t have any additional resources to spend.
My job was taken away once I was charged.
How was their time being taken away from other avenues of my defense not a disadvantage for me?
The ADA continually delayed turning over documents such as medical records.
A search warrant was served to retrieve an item from my property even after my attorney was informed that it was there, and I was told that the ADA would be contacted to retrieve it.
Other trash from the back of my vehicle was represented as something nefarious, even though they never bothered to retrieve the trash that had been saved for them from the residence or took the trash they tried to represent as evidence.
My attorneys never addressed this, even though I repeatedly sent the property overview and asked where she ran to.
One of the gentleman's father works with the police department.
The other also works in some capacity for the city.
A request to retrieve all email communications and telephone calls from this time period would be appropriate.
The second lesser included charge, the vote was 9-3, both in favor of acquittal.

Introduction 
I wanted to start a little better than I did with my last attorney.
Even on the last day of court, he still called me a contractor.
I will attempt to communicate more effectively to ensure that I am not wasting your time looking through materials to ascertain answers that I should have provided upfront.
Work History
Continually performed within the top 15% of Agency employees
Received multiple awards, including 2 Superior Civilian Awards, while deployed to active war zones.
Extensive experience in developing multifunctional teams to solve Department of Defense (DoD) issues impacting the DoD Digital Modernization Strategy
Advisor to C-level equivalent (General/SES) for over ten years
Ability to coordinate integration efforts across multiple DoD components.
I have held a Top Secret / Sensitive Compartmented Information for over 20 years.
SCI clearance investigations involve an additional screening process.
Not everyone with a Top Secret (TS) clearance has SCI access.
You are only eligible for SCI screening if specific duties require access to this information.
This required Single Scope Background Investigations, which are extensive background checks and investigation processes that can take several months or even years to complete.
A single-scope background investigation (SSBI) is the most comprehensive investigation that the government can conduct, in addition to interviews and reviews of financial, criminal, and medical records.
It is designed to assess honesty and integrity by measuring various physiological responses while answering several questions.
I also held additional clearance levels reserved for individuals requiring access to sensitive or compartmented information.
These include Special Access Programs (SAP) created for specific government projects or programs requiring additional screening.
These Control System caveats included GAMMA, TALENT KEYHOLE, HUMINT, and SI.
SI / GAMMA - This sub-control system of SI is for highly sensitive communication intercepts (product or content) * and, therefore, requires the ORCON dissemination marking.
GAMMA may contain compartments identified by a codeword or an identifier of four alphabetic characters.
HUMINT/HCS -This control system is intended to provide enhanced protection to exceptionally fragile clandestine HUMINT sources, methods, and activities based on assessed value, critical nature, and information vulnerability.
TALENT KEYHOLE – Covers space-based IMINT (imagery intelligence), SIGINT (signals intelligence), and MASINT (measurement and signature intelligence) collection platforms; related processing and analysis techniques; and research, design, and operation of these platforms.

Rule 403.
Writing or object used to refresh memory.
(c) Terms and conditions of production and use.
For the purposes of this Article the following definitions are applicable:
(1) Writings and Recordings.
– "Writings" and "recordings" consist of letters, words, sounds, or numbers, or their equivalent, set down by handwriting, typewriting, printing, photostating, photographing, magnetic impulse, mechanical or electronic recording, or other form of data compilation.
– "Photographs" include still photographs, x‑ray films, video tapes, and motion pictures.
A duplicate is admissible to the same extent as an original unless (1) a genuine question is raised as to the authenticity of the original or (2) in the circumstances it would be unfair to admit the duplicate in lieu of the original.
We have no idea what the original is or where it is
(3) Original.
An "original" of a photograph includes the negative or any print therefrom.
If data are stored in a computer or similar device, any printout or other output readable by sight, shown to reflect the data accurately, is an "original."
– A "duplicate" is a counterpart produced by the same impression as the original, or from the same matrix, or by means of photography, including enlargements and miniatures, or by mechanical or electronic re‑recording, or by chemical reproduction, or by other equivalent techniques which accurately reproduce the original.

ln previewing the evidence, counsel
generally
should not (1) refer to inadmissible evidence, (2) 'exaggerate or overstate'
the
evidence, or (3) discuss evidence he expects the other party to introduce."
We conclude that the remark
of
the prosecutor did not violate any of these principles.
The prosecutor's
statement
did not go beyond the proper scope and function of an opening statement.
Therefore,
the trial court did not err in overruling defendant's objection.

Witness Credibility and Relationships


Carmen Love's Testimony: Carmen Love, who is a cousin of the accuser, Lauren Deal, expressed in her interview that she was a survivor of domestic violence and rape but insisted she was non-biased.
Law enforcement took her statements seriously without sufficient scrutiny, potentially biasing the investigation against Ben.
For example, Tiffany's claims about Ben's character and behavior were not corroborated by evidence, yet they influenced Ben's perception during the investigation.
Inconsistencies in Lauren Deal's Statements


Contradictory Accounts: Lauren's statements about the alleged assault are inconsistent.
In her police interviews, she indicated that the incident lasted 2-3 minutes and described being held down.
However, at trial, she mentioned that she was unsure of the duration and implied it might have been shorter.
Additionally, she stated that she had bruises on her arms, but these were not visible in the interrogation video or photographs taken at the hospital.
This raises questions about the accuracy of her claims and her reliability as a witness.
The documents indicate that he did not secure bed linens or other potential exculpatory evidence, which could have provided crucial information regarding the alleged assault.
Instead, he opted only to take photographs of the scene, which is insufficient for a thorough investigation.
Witness Interviews: Law enforcement did not interview key witnesses, such as Carmen Love.
Potential for Coercion and Manipulation


Extortion Attempt: The documentation mentions an attempted extortion of $150,000, which was not investigated by law enforcement.
The fact that this extortion was not pursued suggests a failure in the investigative process and may indicate that the charges were influenced by ulterior motives.
Pressure to Plead: The Assistant District Attorney (ADA), Tiffany Bartholomew, allegedly used misleading statements about DNA evidence to pressure Ben into accepting a plea deal.
For example, she claimed to have his sperm and insisted that he should take a plea deal, which Ben knew to be false.
Physical Evidence and Forensic Analysis


DNA Evidence : The absence of DNA evidence linking Ben to the alleged assault is critical.
The documents indicate that Ben willingly provided his DNA, yet no other men who were with Lauren that night were asked for DNA samples.
Medical Examination : The lack of visible injuries or bruising on Lauren, as well as the absence of a thorough medical examination, calls into question the validity of her claims.
The documents state that medical records were subpoenaed multiple times but were not available on the first day of trial, further complicating the prosecution's case.
Timeline Reconstruction


Discrepancies in Timing : The timeline of events as recounted by various witnesses does not align.
A detailed reconstruction of the timeline based on verifiable evidence is essential to clarify these inconsistencies.
The documents indicate that the detective's prior false testimony was not disclosed, which could provide grounds for dismissing the case or excluding certain evidence.
For example, Carmen's testimony about Lauren's behavior and interactions with Ben is inconsistent with other witnesses' accounts, which could be used to undermine her credibility.
Conclusion
The case against Benjamin S. Allen is riddled with inconsistencies, questionable witness credibility, and significant investigative shortcomings.
There is also a required polygraph.
They should have told me immediately about the accusations she was making.
The allegations she made should have been relayed to me so that I could have restricted her access to the kids until she either recovered or managed contact under supervision, as was the court's direction during our custody case.
If law enforcement had done the slightest amount of investigation, they would have discovered the compromising situation my children were placed in and should have notified me of her accusations so that previous court requirements could have been reinstated for the protection of my children.

Application to Scenario
Impact of Familial Relationship:
Basic Element: Witness credibility and potential conflict of interest.
Giglio v. United States | 405 U.S. 150 (1972)
Importance of witness credibility and prosecutorial disclosure.
Directly relates to the impact of a detective's familial relationship on witness testimony.
This relationship could have been used to impeach Carmen Love's testimony and challenge the integrity of the investigation.
Withholding of video evidence from Schooly's bar that contradicted witness statements.
This video evidence could have been used to challenge the credibility of multiple witnesses and potentially exonerate Mr. Allen.
Examples include:
Lauren Deal's testimony contradicting video evidence from the bar.
(Best v. Duke University, 337 N.C. 742, 448 S.E.2d 506 (1994))
The lack of thorough investigation, apparent bias, and potential fabrication of evidence suggest malice and lack of probable cause.
b) Mischaracterization of Witness Statements: The detective's report includes statements allegedly made by witnesses that are contradicted by their actual recorded statements.
c) False Representation of DNA Evidence: The ADA misrepresented the presence of Mr. Allen's DNA as evidence to pressure him into accepting a plea deal.
This omission is a fundamental flaw in the investigation.
b) Neglect of Physical Evidence: The detective did not collect crucial physical evidence from the alleged crime scene, such as bedsheets or other potential DNA sources.
c) Lack of Timeline Verification: The investigation failed to establish a coherent and verified timeline of events.
The discrepancies in the timeline, particularly the unaccounted hour, were not adequately investigated or explained.
e) Failure to Verify Accuser's Claims: The detective did not adequately verify Lauren Deal's claims about her movements after leaving Mr. Allen's house.
Additionally, we should consider how cognitive biases, such as confirmation bias and tunnel vision, might have influenced the course of this investigation.
Overlooked Techniques and Procedures:

a) Failure to Conduct a Proper Crime Scene Investigation:
Standard crime scene investigation procedures were not followed.
b) Lack of Forensic Analysis:
There's no indication that proper forensic analysis was conducted on the limited evidence that was collected.
This should have included:

DNA analysis of any biological evidence
Toxicology reports to corroborate or refute claims about intoxication levels
Analysis of clothing for transfer evidence

c) Failure to Establish a Comprehensive Timeline:
A detailed timeline of events, corroborated by cell phone records, surveillance footage, and witness statements, was not constructed.
d) Neglect of Electronic Evidence:
There's no indication that investigators sought to obtain or analyze electronic evidence such as:

Cell phone records and geolocation data
Social media activity
Text messages or other communications between involved parties

e) Lack of Follow-Up Interviews:
Key witnesses were not re-interviewed as new information came to light.
Follow-up interviews are crucial for clarifying inconsistencies and addressing new questions that arise during an investigation.
f) Failure to Use Cognitive Interview Techniques:
There's no evidence that cognitive interview techniques, which are known to elicit more accurate and detailed information from witnesses, were employed.
b) Physical Evidence: The lack of immediate physical evidence is striking:
No rape kit was performed immediately
No evidence was collected from the alleged crime scene
No visible injuries were documented on Lauren Deal or Ben Allen
This absence of physical evidence should have prompted a more thorough investigation before an arrest was made.
c) Witness Statements: The statements from other witnesses, particularly Joseph DeMarco and Steve Happel, were not fully consistent with Lauren Deal's account.
These discrepancies should have been resolved before determining probable cause.
d) Video Evidence: The existence of video evidence from Schooly's bar, which apparently contradicted some aspects of the accuser's story, was not considered in the probable cause determination.
Timeline Issues:
The timeline presented by Lauren Deal and corroborated by her mother is inconsistent with objective evidence, particularly the hospital video timestamp.
This discrepancy casts doubt on the entire narrative and should have been a red flag in the probable cause determination.
Lack of Corroboration:
The failure to corroborate key aspects of Lauren Deal's story before making an arrest is a significant flaw in the probable cause determination.
Ignoring Exculpatory Evidence:
The apparent dismissal of evidence that contradicted Lauren Deal's account, such as the video from Schooly's and the statements of other witnesses, is a serious breach of the duty to consider all available evidence in determining probable cause.
This failure to explore other possibilities undermines the validity of the probable cause determination.
Conclusion on Probable Cause:
Based on this analysis, it appears that the standard for probable cause was not met in the arrest of Ben Allen.
The investigation was rushed, key evidence was ignored or not sought, and potential biases were not accounted for.
The totality of the circumstances, when properly considered, does not support a reasonable belief that Mr. Allen committed the alleged crime.
I'll examine this through the lens of both an experienced attorney and detective, looking for key details that could justify or undermine probable cause.
Key Points from the Interview:
Ben Allen voluntarily came to the police station for questioning.
He expresses concern about potential neglect charges for not looking for Lauren in the woods.
In this interview, there's no direct admission of criminal conduct.
His concern about neglect charges suggests awareness something may have happened after leaving the bar, but he doesn't provide details about events at his house.
The interview alone does not appear to provide sufficient grounds for arrest on sexual assault charges.
A thorough review of the complete case file, including Lauren's statement and any physical evidence, would be necessary to make a definitive assessment of probable cause.
Transparency: The detective doesn't clearly communicate to Ben Allen that he's a suspect in a potential crime.
Voluntariness: While Allen came to the station voluntarily, the detective doesn't make it clear that Allen is free to leave at any time.
He's not fully respecting Allen's autonomy or right to informed consent in the interrogation process.

Franks v. Delaware (False Statements in Probable-Cause Submissions)
False Statement: “At 2:00 a.m., Lauren told Carmen she was going with Ben.”
Materiality: The State uses this claim to assert coordinated, voluntary movement and continuity of company—critically shaping probable-cause inferences (e.g., identity of companions, opportunity, continuity, and alleged incapacitation narrative).
Validation: The 2:00 a.m. statement goes to the heart of who went where and with whom; it’s not collateral.

A. Plea-Phase Retaliation / Baseless Aggravator
Threatened to add—and then added—the “position of trust or confidence” aggravator solely if Mr. Allen rejected the plea, despite evidence showing no such relationship.

Omitted disclosure of the detective’s familial tie to witness Carmen Love; failed to interview plainly relevant witnesses (e.g., West and Morrison) and to correct false affidavit portrayals of DeMarco and Love.

Prosecutorial Violations
OFFERING A PLEA DEAL UNDER FALSE PRETENSES
Claim:
ADA Bartholomew admitted in the judges chambers that she misunderstood the DNA evidence when offering a plea deal.
Evidence:
The defendant claims that the ADA offered a plea bargain based on a flawed DNA evidence interpretation.
When the plea was declined, she returned to the Grand Jury to add an aggravating factor to the indictment​.
Evidence:
Discovery was not turned over until the last minute, including during trial​​.
Defense had to file multiple continuances because of insufficient discovery and medical record delays​.
Assertion: Defense requested continuances citing lack of disclosure.
Prejudice: Impaired defense (e.g., DNA expert unable to evaluate evidence fully).
SUPPRESSION OR LATE DISCLOSURE OF EVIDENCE (BRADY VIOLATION)
Claim:
ADA Bartholomew suppressed or disclosed critical evidence inadequately or too late for effective defense use.
Evidence:
DNA and mental health record delays.
The failure to do so constitutes a Brady violation, regardless of intent.
Conclusion:
A viable Brady claim arises from the ADA’s misconduct in evidence management.
SUBORNING PERJURY / KNOWING PRESENTATION OF FALSE TESTIMONY
Claim:
The ADA knowingly relied on Lauren Deal's impeachable testimony, despite prior notice of its unreliability.
Evidence:
Witness inconsistencies are well-documented.
Despite this, the ADA proceeded with the retrial and presented the witness again.
Application:
The ADA had credible knowledge that Lauren Deal committed perjury, as demonstrated by internal contradictions and evidence held by the DA.
In that case, proceeding with her testimony without correction constitutes suborning perjury.
Evidence:
ADA retried the case post-mistrial (12-0, 9-3 for innocence)​.
Reindicted with aggravating factor after plea rejection.
Ignored the defense’s presentation of impeaching evidence.
Application:
The ADA’s actions violated both rules, particularly failing to disclose, misrepresenting the context of the plea, and ignoring impeachment.

Misrepresentation of DNA Evidence: The ADA misrepresented DNA evidence, misleading the court and the jury.

Accuser Statement Reliability Issues: Concerns exist regarding the reliability of accusers' statements used as primary evidence.
Evidence Verification Failures: Lack of Scrutiny
Unverified Accuser Claims: The detective failed to adequately verify the accuser's claims regarding movements after the alleged incident.
Physical Layout Contradiction: Physical evidence and the crime scene layout contradicted the accuser's account, yet these discrepancies were not thoroughly investigated.
Failure to Cross-Examine: Defense attorneys failed to cross-examine key witnesses, missing critical opportunities to challenge testimony.
The defense did not question why witnesses such as Carmen Love were not present at the trial.
Extortion Claims Ignored: Defense counsel did not adequately investigate extortion claims, overlooking potentially exculpatory avenues.
Improper Forensic Evidence: Improper or extremely weak forensic evidence was presented, failing to meet evidentiary standards.
Eyewitness Identification Errors: Potential errors in eyewitness identification were not adequately addressed, contributing to the flawed process.
Brady Violations
Failure to Correct Known False Testimony
The ADA repeatedly refused to correct testimony known to be false, explicitly violating the prosecutors' constitutional obligation to rectify perjured testimony.
Persistent refusal to rectify perjured testimony directly contravenes this standard.
There was no apparent reason for the detective to read this statement as Hoskins was present to testify.
The Detective reading the statement didn’t allow cross-examination and should not have been allowed.
Removal of confusing passages and inconsistencies from the original statement.
Omission of personal feelings and emotional reactions of the witness.
Removal of mentions of other potentially involved individuals.
Additionally, essential crime scene evidence—such as bedding and bathroom trash—was not collected, and no photographs were taken, violating NCGS §15A-268.
Pants allegedly belonging to the accuser were never adequately tested, further undermining probable cause.
Evidentiary Deficiencies: Critical investigative steps were omitted:
Failure to secure physical evidence.
Lack of evaluation of the alleged crime scene.
Inadequate assessment of witness credibility.
Failure to investigate inconsistencies in the accuser's statements.
Misrepresentation of DNA Evidence in Plea Negotiations
False Pretenses for Plea Deal: Coercive Tactics
False DNA Claim: The ADA falsely misrepresented the existence of the defendant's DNA as evidence to coerce the defendant into accepting a plea deal.
Inadequate storage of evidence.
Insufficient documentation of evidence with crime scene information.
Lack of restrictions on who handled the evidence.
Memory loss among witnesses due to extended delays, undermining the reliability of testimony.
Selective focus on evidence that supported the accuser's allegations.
Hospital Video Timestamp Manipulation
Timeline Evidence Alteration: Potential Cover-Up
Timestamp Misrepresentation: Detective Freeman appears to have deliberately misrepresented the timestamp of a hospital video, claiming it was recorded at 3:42 AM when metadata indicated a creation time of 2:42 AM.
Critical Timeline Discrepancy: This one-hour discrepancy is crucial to the timeline of events and raises concerns about:
Potential manipulation of evidence to fit a predetermined narrative.
Fabricated Assault and False Allegations
Conspiracy to Create False Narrative: Deceptive Scheme
Assault Fabrication: Evidence suggests the alleged sexual assault was fabricated and part of a coordinated deceptive scheme involving multiple individuals.
Conspiracy Elements: This conspiracy included:
The evolution of the story over time indicates a constructed narrative.
Inconsistent and changing narratives between interviews, highlighting fabrication.
Financial Motivation for False Accusations
Attempted Bribery Evidence: Financial Gain Incentive
Bribery Attempt: Evidence emerged of a mutual friend offering a substantial bribe ($15,000 per year for 10 years) to make the case "go away," suggesting financial motivation behind the allegations.
Accuser's Financial Circumstances: The accuser's circumstances as a single mother recently evicted from her boyfriend's residence provided a plausible financial motive for fabricating the assault claim to secure financial benefits.
False Evidence Claims: The ADA falsely claimed:
Lab results identified the defendant's DNA/sperm, which was untrue.
Evidence of damage to the victim’s vagina was evident, also untrue.
Deliberate Misrepresentation: These false claims constitute deliberate misrepresentation, likely used to secure the indictment from the Grand Jury based on fabricated information.
Time Gap in the Investigation Timeline
Unexplained Critical Timeline Void: Investigative Neglect
Uninvestigated Time Gap: The detective or attorneys never investigated a significant, unexplained one-hour gap in the timeline of events, representing a critical oversight.
Potential Lost Evidence: This time gap could potentially contain crucial, unexamined information that is highly relevant to the case.
The evidence points to this being a fabrication that should have been investigated by the defense and the district attorney’s office.
Inconsistent Hospital Timeline
Deliberate Timeline Manipulation: Deception Indicated
Hospital Timeline Discrepancies: Major discrepancies exist regarding Lauren's arrival times at Central Carolina Hospital (CCH) and UNC Hospital, suggesting deliberate timeline manipulation.
Unexplained Two-Hour Gap: An unexplained two-hour period remains unaccounted for, raising suspicions of deliberate deception or concealment of critical events during this period.
Security camera timestamps, video footage, and official documents contradict witness accounts of the timeline.
Contradictory Video Evidence Ignored
Exculpatory Surveillance Footage: Evidence Disregarded
Video Evidence Contradiction: Video evidence from Schooly's bar directly contradicted witness statements, yet law enforcement or prosecution did not properly investigate or acknowledge this crucial contradiction.
The contradictory statements and other exaggerations were put into an affidavit to provide the illusion of guilt.
Exculpatory Potential: This video evidence had the potential to significantly challenge the credibility of multiple witnesses and potentially exonerate the defendant, yet was ignored.
Misrepresentation of Evidence in the Opening Statement
Misleading Jury with False Information: Ethical Breach
Opening Statement Misrepresentation: The ADA misrepresented DNA evidence to the jury during her opening statement.
Rehearsed Witness Testimony
Coordinated Witness Preparation: Authenticity Compromised
Rehearsed Testimonies: Evidence suggests that Lauren and her mother's testimonies appeared rehearsed, indicating potential witness coaching and manipulation of their accounts.
Witness Coaching: Witness Steve Happel's account details, observing Lauren receiving explicit coaching for her testimony, raising severe concerns about the authenticity and reliability of their statements.
Missing and Lost Phone Evidence
Critical Evidence Not Preserved: Evidence Handling Failure
Lost Phone and Data: The legal team was entrusted with a phone and an expert’s fee of  $5,000 to extract data from a telephone containing potentially exculpatory text messages, but the phone and the extracted data have been irretrievably lost.
Second Interview Contradictions from Carmen Love
Dramatically Changed Story Between Interviews: Witness Deception
First Interview Denial: In her first interview with Detective Freeman, Carmen Love explicitly denied knowing Ben Allen when directly asked.
Second Interview Reversal: In a subsequent interview with a private investigator, Carmen Love completely contradicted her initial statements, claiming extensive interaction and conversation with Ben Allen at the bar.
This complete reversal in testimony indicates deliberate deception and potential witness tampering or coordination.
Carmen Love's Undisclosed Survivor Status Impact
Biased Witness with Undisclosed Motivations: Impartiality Questioned
Undisclosed Bias: In her second interview, Carmen Love revealed she is a survivor of domestic violence and rape, a critical detail not disclosed in her first interview with law enforcement.
Unexplored Bias: This undisclosed background created a significant and unexamined bias that was never explored or considered during the official investigation, potentially influencing her testimony and perceptions.
Yet, this video was not documented in initial reports or used as evidence for issuing an arrest warrant.
Chain of Custody Neglect: Despite lacking any documented chain of custody, this video evidence was later introduced during court proceedings, raising serious questions about its authenticity and admissibility.
Inconsistent Records Timing: The timing of hospital records appears inconsistent with the physical timeline of events, suggesting potential manipulation or improper maintenance of official medical records.
Missing 911 Records
Critical Emergency Records Not Provided: Transparency Issues
Non-Disclosure of 911 Records: The failure to release 911 records and other relevant documentation from the alleged incident creates valid grounds for questioning the integrity and validity of the initial investigation.
Systematic Failures: Basic investigative steps that should have been routinely taken based on his training and experience were repeatedly and demonstrably ignored throughout this investigation, indicating gross incompetence or deliberate misconduct.
Initial interviews with Deal and Love reveal inconsistencies (e.g., Love denies knowing Allen, and no mention of any invitation by the defendant).
DNA swab consented by Allen; no incriminating results.
Extortion allegations surface (~$150,000 demanded).
Video evidence contradicts statements but is restricted in presentation.
He also gave inconsistent testimony on the arrest process.10
Failure to Establish Probable Cause: No affidavit or notes documented probable cause; reliance on uncorroborated, contradictory statements (e.g., Deal's account biomechanically implausible; Love's initial contradictions).
Elements like Allen's presence, Deal's screaming, and denial fall short of "fair probability" of guilt.11
Key Witness Identities and Connections
Peter West: Present with Lauren Deal at bars; father employed by the Sheriff's Department; local government inspector; connections to the Sheriff and magistrate.12
James Morrison: Carmen Love's boyfriend; city government employee since 2010; similar justice system connections; close ties to Detective Freeman.13
Familial Relationship and Witness Omissions: Detective Freeman, related to witness Carmen Love, did not interview Peter West or James Morrison despite their presence and potential relevance.
His testimony denied knowledge of them, contradicting available evidence (e.g., photos, local common knowledge).
This omission could have deprived the defense of information regarding the accuser's intoxication and behavior, thereby violating Brady v. Maryland, 373 U.S. 83 (1963).
This dereliction suggests bad faith under Arizona v. Youngblood, 488 U.S. 51 (1988).16
Prosecutorial Misconduct
The ADA's conduct raises concerns about fairness, including potential misrepresentations and delays.17
Misrepresentation of DNA Evidence: The ADA allegedly misrepresented DNA evidence in plea talks and added an aggravating factor post-refusal, potentially constituting coercive tactics under the Fourteenth Amendment.
Witness statements (e.g., Carmen Love's) evolved, raising credibility questions (e.g., from denial to detailed familiarity).18
Selective Witness Interviewing and Procedural Abuse: Excessive 37 continuances over four years caused undue hardship (e.g., lost phone data, witness memory fade, economic impact on Allen).
Contradictions in Deal's account (e.g., impossible escape, no woods/run, 75% illumination vs. "pitch black") not examined.24
Accuser Statement Reliability: Initial focus on "feet hurt," not assault; no "rape" mentioned.
Contradicted by video (e.g., no pre-departure interaction with Allen).25
Chain of Custody Problems: Documents replaced at trial; edited witness statements (e.g., Hoskins') violated hearsay rules and Confrontation Clause under Crawford v. Washington, 541 U.S. 36 (2004).26
Unverified Claims: Deal's outrunning fit soldiers implausible; physical layout contradictions ignored.27
Defense Representation Issues
The defendant suffered from ineffective assistance, undermining fair defense under Strickland v. Washington, 466 U.S. 668 (1984).28
Failure to Cross-Examine: No questioning on Love's absence or inconsistencies.
Extortion Claims Ignored: Private detective ordered not to pursue $150,000 demand.
Loss of Data: Phone records with exculpatory info lost; initial interviews vanished.
These failures prejudiced the outcome, as post-trial juror feedback indicated that knowledge of the extortion attempt would have led to immediate acquittal.
Disclosure must occur timely manner; here, it did not.29
Types: Negating guilt (e.g., video contradictions); impeachment (e.g., conflicts); discrediting police (e.g., Freeman's perjury).
Economic and Emotional Harm
Significant Prejudice: Loss of income, job termination, emotional distress to family; witness memory loss.
No conviction occurred, and retrial may be unwarranted given weaknesses.

## [PROPOSAL] STRATEGIC THEME 2
- **Evidence Count**: 445 items linked
- **Key Identifiers**:

Investigative Shortcomings


Lack of Evidence Collection: Detective Steve Freeman's failure to collect physical evidence from the alleged crime scene is a significant oversight.
Legal and Ethical Considerations


Brady and Giglio Violations : The prosecution's failure to disclose evidence that could impeach the credibility of witnesses, particularly Detective Freeman, may constitute violations of Brady and Giglio.
Specific instances in this case include:
Failure to disclose the familial relationship between Detective Freeman and Carmen Love, a key witness.
Detective Freeman's potentially false testimony about the timeline of events, particularly regarding the hospital video timestamp.
c) Malicious Prosecution: The actions of Detective Freeman and the ADA may constitute malicious prosecution.
Misrepresentation of Evidence:
a) Manipulation of Video Evidence: Detective Freeman appears to have misrepresented the timestamp of the hospital video, claiming it was recorded at 3:42 AM when metadata shows it was created at 2:42 AM.
Bad Investigative Techniques:
a) Failure to Conduct Thorough Interviews: Detective Freeman failed to interview key witnesses, including Peter West and James Morrison, who were present at Schooly's.
d) Biased Approach to Investigation: Detective Freeman's approach shows signs of confirmation bias, where he appears to have focused on evidence that supported the accuser's claims while ignoring or failing to pursue evidence that might exonerate Mr. Allen.
§ 242 - Deprivation of Rights Under Color of Law:
The actions of Detective Freeman and potentially the ADA may violate this federal statute, which makes it a crime for a person acting under color of any law to willfully deprive a person of a right or privilege protected by the Constitution or laws of the United States.
Rushed Investigation:
Detective Freeman's decision to arrest Mr. Allen after only a few hours of investigation, without thoroughly examining all available evidence or interviewing all potential witnesses, suggests a rush to judgment that is incompatible with a proper probable cause determination.
Potential Bias:
The familial relationship between Detective Freeman and Carmen Love introduces a potential bias that should have disqualified Freeman from making the probable cause determination.
Failure to Consider Alternative Explanations:
There's no evidence that Detective Freeman seriously considered alternative explanations for Lauren Deal's allegations, such as consensual activity or false accusation.
To assess probable cause for arrest, I'll need to carefully analyze the interview content, apply relevant legal principles, and consider the totality of the circumstances known to Detective Freeman at the time.
The key question is what additional information Detective Freeman had beyond this interview to establish probable cause.
Potential Issues:
Lack of specifics about events at Allen's house
No mention of sexual contact or assault
Allen's voluntary cooperation
Absence of physical evidence mentioned
To justify the arrest, Detective Freeman would need additional evidence not presented in this interview, such as:
Lauren's statement alleging assault
Physical evidence supporting the allegation
Witness corroboration of key events
Inconsistencies in Allen's account compared to other evidence
Conclusion:
Based solely on this interview, there does not appear to be probable cause for arrest on sexual assault charges.
