The questioning became focused on potential criminal activity

INVESTIGATOR Ethical Concerns of THE Allen Case
The investigator’s conduct, Detective Steve Freeman of the Lee County Sheriff’s Office,  introduces complex legal and ethical issues that could significantly impact the case.
Here’s a detailed analysis of the various aspects:
Conflict of Interest with the Investigator:
Legal Aspect: Detective Freeman, a witness's family member, introduces a conflict of interest.
The familial relationship between Detective Freeman and Carmen Love already undermines the case's credibility.
The report necessitates a comprehensive inquiry into the actions of Detective Steve Freeman, the Assistant District Attorney (ADA) Tiffany Bartholomew, and each entity that comprises the Lee County judicial framework.
Investigative Failures and Detective Misconduct
As detailed, Detective Freeman's investigation is not simply inadequate; it appears to be fundamentally compromised by bias and a deliberate disregard for established protocol.
Detective Bias: The undisclosed familial relationship between Detective Freeman and Carmen Love, a key witness, immediately triggers a profound ethical alarm.
Freeman's failure to disclose this relationship, coupled with his reliance on Love's evolving and demonstrably inconsistent statements, exposes a calculated manipulation of the investigative process.
Freeman's tenuous excuse – claiming they were not present at the 'incident' despite video evidence placing them with the accuser earlier – is transparently disingenuous.
Detective Freeman's testimony reveals a shocking dereliction of duty.
To ensure a pre-determined outcome, Freeman's extensive training and experience render his procedural lapses not as incompetence but as a calculated disregard for proper procedure.
False Statements: Detective Freeman's affidavit is riddled with demonstrable falsehoods regarding the timeline, witness statements, and events surrounding the alleged incident.
Freeman’s conflicting priorities, such as attending his brother’s wedding, influenced this decision, as he preferred not to engage in a formal investigation that evening.
For instance, Freeman’s connection to the case, such as his family members allowing him to attend his brother’s wedding, motivated a delay in reporting and investigation.
Coercive Tactics: 
Selective Witness Interviewing:The report reveals a pattern of selective witness interviews conducted by the ADA, mirroring Detective Freeman's approach and exacerbated by substantial discovery violations.
Failure to Investigate Extortion Claims:
Attorney Conflict of Interest: The alleged conflict of interest arising from the defense attorney's previous relationship with Detective Freeman is deeply concerning.
Network of Improper Relationships: The connection between Detective Freeman and the defendant's attorney and their history of collaborative casework, coupled with the familial and social ties within local law enforcement and government, raises serious concerns about a potential network of improper relationships influencing the administration of justice.
This case demands a thorough and independent investigation into the allegations of misconduct against Detective Freeman and the ADA and the broader systemic issues within the Lee County Sheriff’s Department and the judicial framework.
Freeman’s Background and Experience
Freeman’s experience spans nearly three decades in law enforcement.
Freeman is a Captain with the Lee County Sheriff's Office, responsible for Professional Standards and Internal Investigations, which includes oversight of hiring and internal investigations​.
Initial Steps and Involvement in the Case
Freeman was initially contacted while attending his brother’s wedding regarding a sexual assault report filed by Lauren Deal.
On October 19, 2019, Freeman was informed of the alleged sexual assault while at his brother’s wedding.
This sequence of events clearly indicates that Freeman took charge of the investigation and was likely the key decision-maker in subsequent procedural matters, such as evidence collection, interviews, and determining the next steps.
Freeman’s Interaction with Key Individuals
Freeman’s interactions with Deal and Allen, as well as other individuals involved, are as follows:
Interview with Lauren Deal:
Freeman interviewed Deal that same day in a room equipped with audio and video recording capabilities.
Freeman interviewed him in a separate room from where he had interviewed Deal earlier.
This interview room was equipped with audio and video recording capabilities, and Freeman started recording by pressing a button outside the door.
During the interview, Freeman asked Allen about his interactions with Deal on the night of October 18.
Freeman asked Allen to sign a consent form for a buccal swab (DNA sample), which Allen agreed to and signed.
Freeman then collected the buccal swab and documented it as evidence.
Interviews with Other Individuals:
Freeman contacted Joe DeMarco to obtain details of the case and further contact information for Steve Happel.
The phone interviews with Freeman on October 19 were recorded, although he noted they were reluctant to participate fully​.
Freeman also interviewed Tiffany Allen and Roger Hoskins on October 31, with Hoskins later providing a written and signed statement.
Freeman recorded Hoskins’ statement, obtained his signature, and also typed a formal version of Hoskins' statement for clarity and verification.
Both Hoskins and Freeman signed this typed statement, which Freeman then documented as evidence​.
Freeman additionally reviewed text messages and digital evidence from Deal and friends Tiffany Allen and Carmen Love, which were pertinent to the timeline and context of the reported events​.
These interactions built Freeman’s case and informed his conclusions regarding probable cause, but they also revealed omissions in documentation and custody procedures, particularly concerning the arrest of Benjamin Allen, without any cross-referencing of details received.
Collection and Documentation of Evidence
Evidence collected and managed by Freeman includes:
Physical Evidence: Freeman and Lieutenant Smith later visited Allen's residence at 94 Beacon Circle to check for any items she left behind.
Freeman did not seize the items immediately, as he would have needed either a search warrant or the resident’s consent.
Freeman retrieved Deal’s medical records and her Sexual Assault Evidence Collection Kit (SAECK) from UNC Hospital Police.
DNA Sample: Freeman obtained Allen’s consent for a buccal swab, which he documented as evidence.
Video Surveillance: Freeman reviewed hours of surveillance footage from Schooly’s Bar, which showed interactions between Deal, Allen, and others.
This footage further informed Freeman’s understanding of the evening’s events
Search Warrant: Following interviews with Tiffany Allen and Roger Hoskins, Freeman sought a search warrant for the defendant's residence (94 Beacon Circle) based on Deal’s account and the information gathered through interviews.
Freeman executed the search warrant on October 24, with Detective Marcum assisting.
On October 24, Freeman photographed the residence and documented any items, ultimately photographing and seizing black pants.
Freeman strangely determined they were not likely to yield further valuable physical evidence but did not identify how he could decide they were the accusers​.
Freeman did not process any part of what would be assessed as the crime scene.
Freeman’s careful steps in securing certain types of evidence (such as DNA) contrast with his lack of documentation in other areas, such as probable cause for the defendant’s detention.
Probable Cause and Lack of Documentation
Arrest Warrant Issuance:
After compiling evidence, Freeman verbally presented his findings to a magistrate, who provided a Magistrate’s Order stating:
I, the undersigned, find that the defendant named above has been arrested without a warrant and the defendant's detention is justified because there is probable cause to believe that on or about the date of offense shown and in the county named above the defendant named above unlawfully, willfully and feloniously did ravish and carnally know LAUREN N. D. by force and against victims will.
The magistrate’s specific language in the order suggests that Allen was already in custody before Freeman presented his findings verbally to the magistrate.
This is reinforced by the messages the defendant sent when Freeman went to see the magistrate and left the defendant with his phone.
"He said he was going to work something for me":
This statement indicates that the defendant had been led to believe, likely by law enforcement (presumably Detective Freeman), that some arrangement might be made to avoid immediate detention or reduce the severity of his situation.
This step is standard practice for someone in Freeman’s position and would be well within his knowledge and experience.
Challenges to Officer Credibility: In court, officers with extensive experience, like Freeman, are generally expected to follow protocols meticulously.
Freeman’s lack of documentation, despite his experience and knowledge, should lead a judge or jury to question his investigation's reliability and integrity.
Freeman’s Decision Against Probable Cause Documentation
Explanations and Implications: For an officer with Freeman’s experience, neglecting to document probable cause is a highly unusual choice.
Possible explanations include:
Deliberate Avoidance: Freeman may have deliberately avoided documentation to bypass judicial oversight or to expedite the defendant’s detention.
Unintentional Oversight: Although less likely given his background, it’s possible Freeman unintentionally omitted this step, though his repeated evasiveness in testimony about the defendant’s custody timing makes this seem improbable.
Perception of Sufficient Evidence without Documentation: Freeman may have believed his verbal description to the magistrate (if any was given) sufficient to establish probable cause.
Avoiding Examination: Freeman’s repeated avoidance of the questions during his testimony shows an awareness that the defendant’s initial detention without a warrant did not adhere to procedure.
Given his experience, Freeman recognized that any perceived deviation, such as detaining a suspect without judicial authorization, would introduce scrutiny over whether proper protocols were followed.
By eventually stating that the defendant was taken into custody “after” presenting evidence, Freeman attempted to convey the appearance of adherence to typical process, even though the magistrate’s documentation indicates otherwise.
The defendant was never taken before a magistrate; there was no judicial review of Freeman’s decision to arrest, which infringes on the suspect’s rights and bypasses a crucial safeguard against unlawful detention.
Given Freeman’s extensive experience—27 years in law enforcement and his role as an instructor—his omission of details regarding the “without a warrant” arrest authorized by the magistrate seems notable.
In typical law enforcement procedure, especially for someone with Freeman’s background, the expectation would be:
Detailed Documentation and Testimony: A detective would mention whether he formally requested a warrant or if, instead, he presented evidence and established probable cause directly to the magistrate, who then issued an order for custody based on probable cause.
Understanding of Arrest Processes: Freeman’s experience implies a strong understanding of the difference between arrests conducted with warrants and those based on probable cause without warrants.
Given the magistrate’s order specifically stating that the defendant was arrested "without a warrant," Freeman’s testimony omits a crucial procedural detail.
Implications for Lawful Detention: Since Freeman’s explanation does not mention the magistrate’s unique “arrest without a warrant” order, this raises questions about whether he thoroughly clarified the basis for the defendant’s detention, which is a critical point given the legal standards that apply to probable cause arrests.
In summary, Freeman’s testimony does not address why the arrest deviated from the standard procedure (e.g., obtaining a formal warrant), which, given his role, could be interpreted as an incomplete explanation of events surrounding the defendant’s detention.
Freeman avoided questions about when the defendant was taken into custody, and the lack of documentation indicates he knew the process deviated from the norm and sought to downplay or obscure the sequence.
Steve Freeman knew that the detention did not meet standard legal requirements.
For a seasoned officer and instructor like Freeman, not documenting probable cause or taking the suspect before a magistrate is highly irregular, especially when he fully knows the importance of these steps.
Application to Freeman’s Actions: Under these standards, Freeman’s failure to document probable cause could be seen as a failure to meet the requirements for lawful detention.
Freeman’s Training and Expertise: Given Freeman’s extensive background, he would be fully aware of these requirements, particularly given his role as an instructor.
Potential Outcomes and Legal Consequences of Freeman’s Omission
Suppression of Evidence: The defense could file a motion to suppress evidence obtained following Allen’s arrest, arguing that the lack of documented probable cause rendered the arrest unlawful.
Questioning Freeman’s Conduct: Freeman’s failure to document probable cause could be used to question the validity of the entire investigation.
Impact on Future Investigations and Oversight: Procedural deviations in this case could lead to greater oversight or policy changes within Freeman’s department, particularly if it’s determined that officers are not consistently following documentation standards.
Summary of Key Points
Freeman’s failure to document probable cause for Allen’s arrest represents a significant procedural deviation, especially given his experience and knowledge of legal standards.
Raises questions about Freeman’s credibility and adherence to protocol, potentially affecting the outcome of the case.
This procedural gap calls Freeman’s investigative integrity into question and could influence how evidence and his testimony are perceived by the court.
Rather than approving probable cause before custody (the norm), this retrospective order served as a post hoc justification for the detention already initiated by Freeman.
Application to Freeman’s Actions: Freeman’s decision to detain Allen without first securing a warrant appears to deviate from these established standards.
By detaining Allen first and seeking approval after, Freeman effectively bypassed the standard judicial review process.
Reliance on Verbal Justification (If Applicable): If Freeman presented probable cause verbally without documentation, the magistrate would have had only Freeman’s description to go on, without the support of written evidence.
Without a warrant, the custody is based solely on Freeman’s assertion of probable cause.
Retrospective Justification as a Procedural Weakness: A retrospective order bypasses the pre-detention safeguard of probable cause review, meaning Allen’s detention was based on Freeman’s judgment alone without prior judicial approval.
How Freeman’s Experience Factors Into This Unusual Process
Expectations Based on Experience: Freeman’s long history in law enforcement, including teaching law enforcement procedures, indicates he would be well aware of both probable cause requirements and the importance of prompt judicial review.
Possible Misinterpretation or Misuse of Authority: Freeman’s decision to proceed with Allen’s detention without prior judicial review could reflect either a misinterpretation of his authority or an assumption that his judgment would suffice.
Credibility and Procedural Integrity: Freeman’s decision to pursue retrospective approval could raise doubts about his adherence to protocol, particularly in light of his evasive testimony regarding Allen’s custody timing.
This casts further scrutiny on Freeman’s judgment and adherence to established legal standards.
Freeman’s failure to provide documented probable cause further weakens the procedural legitimacy of the detention, as verbal explanations alone lack accountability.

For instance, she claimed to have seen Lauren talking to unfamiliar men at Schooly's, but this contradicts Joseph Demarco and Steve Happel's statements that they met Lauren for the first time after Carmen had left.
This inconsistency suggests that Carmen's narrative may be influenced by her relationship with the detective and her desire to align with familial expectations.
Tiffany Allen's Influence: Tiffany Allen, Ben's estranged wife, had a history of mental illness and had made unsubstantiated accusations against him, including false claims of child abuse.
The documentation indicates that Tiffany had been diagnosed with severe mental health issues, which were recognized by multiple professionals.
Behavioral Observations: Witnesses described Lauren as being overly intoxicated at the bar, with Steve Happel stating that she was acting hysterical and calling them "assholes."
This behavior contrasts sharply with her portrayal of herself as a victim who was coherent and aware of her surroundings during the alleged assault.
The discrepancy in her behavior before and after the incident suggests that her recollection may be influenced by her state of intoxication and emotional distress.
The lack of follow-up with Carmen, who was present at the bar and had a close relationship with Lauren, deprived the investigation of critical context and corroboration for Ben's defense.
This attempt to coerce Ben into paying off Lauren raises serious questions about the motivations behind the allegations.
For instance, Carmen claims to have seen Lauren talking to unfamiliar men just as she was leaving the bar, while Joseph and Steve state they met Lauren for the first time after Carmen had left.
Additionally, Lauren's arrival at Ben's house is placed at around 2:30 AM, but the timeline provided by other witnesses suggests a different sequence of events.
We were separated, she was on heavy medication for Stage 4 lung cancer, and she was severely mentally ill. She brought up previous accusations about abuse of our children.
The fact that this wasn’t done put my children at risk.
Since we were separated, I was unaware of her state of mind.
I had let her borrow my phone.
It was returned when she passed away.
It was $5,000 out of my pocket and possibly the smoking gun on me being set up.
Her tactic of delay has the intended impact.

Too Neat in the Emotional Arc
She moves seamlessly from:
A fact-like statement (“they knew they couldn’t go to the hospital”)
To a dramatic perception (“he was just as scared as I was”)
To an exact, cinematic quote (“my girlfriend would kill me if I didn’t help you”)
That progression is tidy in a way spontaneous recollection usually isn’t — especially under courtroom questioning.
It feels constructed to hit emotional beats.
Ironically, when a witness recalls an exact turn of phrase from a casual conversation during a traumatic moment — especially years later — it often suggests story reinforcement over time, rather than raw memory.

Other Discrepancies:
Deal’s Demeanor and Actions: Deal described herself as tipsy, giggling, and laughing, yet the video shows her as visibly intoxicated—yelling, walking around barefoot, and stumbling.
This discrepancy between her self-reported behavior and what is actually seen on video further challenges her reliability.
Departure from the Bar: Deal testified that she left with Allen, DeMarco, and Happel, and was aware they’d be traveling in Allen’s truck with DeMarco driving.
However, the video shows she left alone, making it impossible for any conversation about a designated driver in Allen’s truck to have taken place.

I even talked to Amy on the phone to encourage her to let her know it would be ok.
I think this was all a ploy to distract me and get information about how she could report me for cheating on her.
I didn’t think about his until later.
They asked all kinds of questions, talked about how Amy used devices around the house to spy on him, how bad he treated her, all kinds of stuff that still just seems like WAY too similar to be a coincidence.
Mid November 2015 – I got a call at when I left work with Tiffany screaming.
She said Lukas was hurt bad and Morgan also.
I asked what happened but she just said, “I hate you!
This is all your fault!” she then hung up on me.
I tried to call a couple of times.
She answered once and said something about Lukas’s eye.
I got home and went to see the kids.
They were pretty scuffed up but seemed ok.  Lukas had road rash on his face, arm and leg.
Morgan was scraped up on her leg and said her crotch hurt.
I immediately put them in my car and Tiff and I went to the Emergicare in Sanford by the PapaJohn’s.
They checked out and the doctor said they looked ok.
I asked Tiffany what had happened when I had gotten home.
She said Morgan had kept bugging her about riding the go-cart and she was trying to talk on the phone so she couldn’t deal with it.
She said she got tired of hearing it so she said that she could ride it with Lukas.
I couldn’t believe what I was hearing.
She said it was my fault since I had bought it for them…  Morgan was asking because no one was supposed to be on it unless one of us was outside.
Everyone knew this…that is why she asked.
All Tiffany had to do was go outside with her and show her the area they were restricted to riding since Brendan and Carter had their accident.
They were only allowed to ride in a circle in the front yard.
Morgan was asking – following the rules.
I don’t understand why Tiff let her ride it or how it became my fault when I wasn’t even home.
NOV 30th 2014– Tiffany’s parents were in for Thanksgiving.
When I got up Tiffany and her mother were sitting at the table.
I asked where Dan (her step-father) was at.
She said that he was out getting the RV ready for their trip.
I went outside to assist if I could.
Everything seemed a little different but no one was saying much.
I just assumed it was because they were leaving after staying the week of Thanksgiving.
The kids were getting in the RV.
Tiff said that they were going to ride down the road with her parents and that she would pick them up.
I said that she could ride with them also and I would come get them instead of her driving separate.
I could stay and she would go get them.
She didn’t come back for hours.
I texted her a couple of times when it started to get late.
She responded with something and she came home a while later.
This is when she announced to me that she had listened to recordings with her mother and father that contained “proof” that I was abusing the children.
She said that Dan didn’t believe it but he couldn’t wait to get out of there.
The morning started making a little more sense.
She said that she had spent the day at the Sherriff’s office with a detective and the FBI.
She said that she had turned over recordings, my computer, etc.
We argued for a few minutes.
I finally gave up trying to talk to her.
I said that whatever she was going through that I would help her through it.
At this point I went into the living room to get away from the situation.
She came in crying saying she was sorry and didn’t know why I loved her so much.
I let her lay there but told her that I didn’t really feel like touching her.
We ended up going to bed together about an hour later.
She laid down in bed with me and we tried to sleep.
The kids were getting up from bed so I just asked them all to grab their stuff so they could come in the room with us.
They had heard us arguing earlier and she had accused me of abuse so I thought that it would be good if we all slept in the room together.
She got up the next morning and flipped out about all the kids being in the room.
I didn’t get this since she was talking to them when they were bringing their covers and pillows into the room.
She acted like she wasn’t aware that they were there the entire night.
I received a call when I got out of work from Diana Anderson (DSS) asking me to stay at a hotel.
She wanted to do an intake interview before I could go back into the house.
I located a hotel and rented a room.
After work I drive to Sanford to meet with Diana Anderson.
After the intake she told me that I could go back to the house.
She called Tiffany to ask her if it was ok.
I could hear Tiffany disagreeing with that.
Tiffany said that her parents would pay for the hotel room if I didn’t come home.
I didn’t want to make things worse so I agreed to stay in a hotel again.
Since this was the last night on the Safety Plan I thought that it would give Tiffany time to calm down.
I didn’t see anything good coming from me being at the house with her in that state of mind.
When I got home no one was there.
I called Tiffany’s mother and she didn’t answer.
I then called Tiffany’s step-father.
He answered and I told him my concerns about the children not being there.
We both know that Tiffany has mental issues.
About the time that I hung up, Tiffany called.
She said that she wasn’t coming home.
She was saying that Carter thought that I was going to come into the house and kill everyone.
She then said that she was getting a police escort.
I waited for her to get home with the escort.
She didn’t show for a while so I called dispatch asking if the officer would come by the house.
Officer Brewer called me saying that he was on his way.
He told me that Tiffany was going to a hotel.
Since there was no order of any kind for me not to be there, he said it was ok for me to stay.
I asked if it ok to enter the house and he said that it was fine.
I went inside and Tiffany began to text me.
She said that I wasn’t supposed to be at the house due to the order that I signed at DSS.
I explained that it wasn’t true.
She was getting upset so I just stopped texting her.
They had no record of me, Tiffany or my children.
She said that even if it was approved that I didn’t know where she was anyway.
I had told her during our discussion that this was the case.
I left to go get some breakfast since I wasn’t getting anywhere.
I was driving down the road when I got a text from my boss.
This was by the hotel that we had stayed in when we first came to Sanford.
I thought that I would check to see if my kids were there.
I drove through the parking lot and left.
I immediately received a text from Tiffany asking what I was doing there.
After about 10-15 minutes the lady at the desk received a call.
I could hear Tiff on the other end of the line.
She was telling the lady that I was outside her hotel room.
The lady asked her if she had contacted the police, what kind of car, etc.
About the time that Tiffany got off the phone, Diana was available to see me.
I met with her briefly before going back down to the courthouse.
I told her where I was at and why.
I was sitting outside the courthouse when Tiffany pulled in with the kids.
I saw her walking around the front of the building.
I assumed she didn’t know where the sheriff’s office was located.
I walked around the front but realized that I had my phone in my pocket.
I returned it to my car and then went back around the front.
I entered and talked to the kids a moment before being arrested.
DEC 5th – 13th 20014– I stayed with a friend down in Fayetteville during this time.
He was getting ready to deploy so I couldn’t stay with him that long before he had to leave.
DEC 14th thru the 18th 2014– My mother came in so we stayed at a hotel this week.
Tiffany and mom communicated but mostly she was telling mom that she couldn’t see the kids.
DEC 19th 2014- My mom had been in town all week and hadn't had a chance to see the kids.
She had been talking with Tiff all week trying to figure out when she could come by.
My mother had went to the house on the first night and Tiffany wouldn't let her see them or let her in the house.
By Friday we were ready to leave so we could do Christmas back home in KY.
(Psychologist recommended through work to help me deal with the situation)  Mom decided that she was going to go by the house to see the kids.
She asked me about it and I said that it would be ok since she wasn't restricted by the conditions of my release.
I thought that it would be a good idea to drop off the presents since the kids could have them for Christmas and it would give her more room in her trunk if we stopped to finish up shopping in Nashville.
(We didn't end up going that way home.)
I was at the gas station across from the Tramway shopping center when mom got to our house.
She said they were getting ready to leave.
I thought that I could grab a couple of things if they weren't going to be there.
Mom called me back and said that my ex-wife had come out on the porch.
I said that my ex-wife was there and didn't know how this was going to go.
The dispatcher told me that someone would meet me at Beacon Circle.
Beacon Circle is really close to the house so I drove to the end of Aviation Lane to meet the officer and take advisement from there.
I still had about 40 minutes before my appointment but it was getting close to whether I could grab some stuff before leaving or not.
Next thing I know Tiffany pulls up beside me and starts cussing and yelling at me.
Essentially all hell broke loose.
Our dog comes running up the road, the van door opens and I see my oldest son crying, (I found out later that he had broken his wrist) mom is out of the car beside the van.
Tiff grabs my mom (left bruises on her arms - she is 65) and is yelling along my ex-wife are yelling.
(HWY1)  I get out of the car and tell him that my ex-wife left with my son.
I didn't know what else to say.
I was pretty shaken up about what had just happened and seeing my ex-wife there.
I had no idea why she was there and assumed that she was going to leave with Brendan.
That wouldn't have been good in my opinion.
I did ask my son if he was ok when the van door opened.
Mom asked him if he wanted to come with Nana and he said that it was fine - he would stay.
I left immediately to go back to KY.  We stayed at a hotel somewhere in NC.
No one was allowed to talk to kids – not even their cousins.
I was able to get visitation at this point.
I got to see the kids that night.
My mother was able to go to pick up the kids so they could come see me.
JAN 28th 2015– I found out later that Sara had contacted DSS about her concerns about Tiffany.
She came over that evening to take my statement.
She said that Brendan and Lukas claimed that I had abused them.
I got more information on this later from Sara who had stayed in the house with Tiffany at multiple times over the past few weeks.
FEB 3rd – I went with Sara to DSS today.
She told DSS a bunch of things that happened while she was there that changed her mind about what was going on.
It was hard to listen too.
I got to meet the foster parents.
We were separated, she was on heavy medication for Stage 4 lung cancer, and she was severely mentally ill. She brought up previous accusations about abuse of our children.
The fact that this wasn’t done put my children at risk.
Since we were separated, I was unaware of her state of mind.
I had let her borrow my phone.
It was returned when she passed away.
It was $5,000 out of my pocket and possibly the smoking gun on me being set up.
Her tactic of delay has the intended impact.
